   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Smartphone
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      "Smartphones" redirects here. For the song by Trey Songz, see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SmartPhones_(song)" title="SmartPhones (song)">
       SmartPhones (song)
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Not to be confused with
      <a href="/wiki/Feature_phone" title="Feature phone">
       Feature phone
      </a>
      .
     </div>

       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2550" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg/200px-MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg/300px-MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg/400px-MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MSC_2014_Smartphone-Audience_Mueller_MSC2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A person using a smartphone to take a digital photograph.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <b>
       smartphone
      </b>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">
       mobile phone
      </a>
      (also known as cell phones) with an advanced
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">
       mobile operating system
      </a>
      which combines features of a
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">
       personal computer
      </a>
      operating system with other features useful for mobile or handheld use.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phonescoop-smartphone_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-smartphone-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phonescoop-featurephone_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-featurephone-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smartphones, which are usually pocket-sized, typically combine the features of a mobile phone, such as the abilities to place and receive voice calls and create and receive
      <a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">
       text messages
      </a>
      , with those of other popular digital
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_device" title="Mobile device">
       mobile devices
      </a>
      like
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">
       personal digital assistants
      </a>
      (PDAs), such as an event calendar,
      <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">
       media player
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_games" title="Video games">
       video games
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/GPS_navigation_device#Mobile_phones_with_GPS_hapability" title="GPS navigation device">
       GPS navigation
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Camera_phone" title="Camera phone">
       digital camera
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_video_camera" title="Digital video camera">
       digital video camera
      </a>
      . Most smartphones can access the
      <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
       Internet
      </a>
      and can run a variety of
      <a href="/wiki/Third-party_software_component" title="Third-party software component">
       third-party software components
      </a>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">
       apps
      </a>
      "). They typically have a color
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flat-panel_display" title="Flat-panel display">
       display
      </a>
      with a
      <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">
       graphical user interface
      </a>
      that covers 70% or more of the front surface. The display is often a
      <a href="/wiki/Touchscreen" title="Touchscreen">
       touchscreen
      </a>
      , which enables the user to use a
      <a href="/wiki/Virtual_keyboard" title="Virtual keyboard">
       virtual keyboard
      </a>
      to type words and numbers and press onscreen icons to activate "app" features.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1999, the Japanese firm
      <a href="/wiki/NTT_DoCoMo" title="NTT DoCoMo">
       NTT DoCoMo
      </a>
      released the first smartphones to achieve mass adoption within a country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smartphones became widespread in the late 2000s. Most of those produced from 2012 onward have high-speed mobile broadband
      <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">
       4G LTE
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Motion_detector" title="Motion detector">
       motion sensors
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_payment" title="Mobile payment">
       mobile payment
      </a>
      features. In the third quarter of 2012, one billion smartphones were in use worldwide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Don_Reisinger_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Don_Reisinger-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Global smartphone sales surpassed the sales figures for regular cell phones in early 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news1_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-news1-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2013, 65% of mobile consumers in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      owned smartphones.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jon_Fingas_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jon_Fingas-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By January 2016, smartphones held over 79% of the U.S. mobile market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan2016_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jan2016-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

         <span class="tocnumber">
          9
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          Other terms
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">
        <a href="#See_also">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          10
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          See also
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">
        <a href="#Notes_and_references">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          11
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          Notes and references
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">
       Early years
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caller_ID_receiver.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="680" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/220px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/330px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/440px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caller_ID_receiver.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The first caller identification receiver (1971).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Devices that combined telephony and
      <a href="/wiki/Computing" title="Computing">
       computing
      </a>
      were first conceptualized by
      <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">
       Nikola Tesla
      </a>
      in 1909 and
      <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Paraskevakos" title="Theodore Paraskevakos">
       Theodore Paraskevakos
      </a>
      in 1971 and patented in 1974, and were offered for sale beginning in 1993. Paraskevakos was the first to introduce the concepts of intelligence,
      <a href="/wiki/Data_processing" title="Data processing">
       data processing
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_display_screen" title="Visual display screen">
       visual display screens
      </a>
      into telephones. In 1971, while he was working with
      <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">
       Boeing
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">
       Huntsville, Alabama
      </a>
      , Paraskevakos demonstrated a
      <a href="/wiki/Transmitter" title="Transmitter">
       transmitter
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Receiver_(radio)" title="Receiver (radio)">
       receiver
      </a>
      that provided additional ways to communicate with remote equipment, however it did not yet have general purpose
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PDA" title="PDA">
       PDA
      </a>
      applications in a wireless device typical of smartphones. They were installed at Peoples' Telephone Company in
      <a href="/wiki/Leesburg,_Alabama" title="Leesburg, Alabama">
       Leesburg, Alabama
      </a>
      and were demonstrated to several telephone companies. The original and historic working models are still in the possession of Paraskevakos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paraskevakos_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-paraskevakos-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Forerunner">
       Forerunner
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Forerunner">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1615" height="316" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/170px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/255px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/340px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/IBM_Simon" title="IBM Simon">
         IBM Simon
        </a>
        and charging base (1994).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
         <a href="#cite_note-10">
          [10]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first mobile phone to incorporate PDA features was an
      <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
       IBM
      </a>
      prototype developed in 1992 and demonstrated that year at the
      <a href="/wiki/COMDEX" title="COMDEX">
       COMDEX
      </a>
      computer industry trade show. It included PDA features and other visionary mobile applications such as maps, stock reports and news. A refined version was marketed to consumers in 1994 by
      <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">
       BellSouth
      </a>
      under the name
      <a href="/wiki/IBM_Simon" title="IBM Simon">
       Simon Personal Communicator
      </a>
      . The Simon was the first commercially available device that could be properly referred to as a "smartphone", although it was not called that in 1994.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bus_week_2012_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bus_week_2012-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneidawind_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-schneidawind-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition to placing and receiving cellular calls, Simon could send and receive
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faxes" title="Faxes">
       faxes
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emails" title="Emails">
       emails
      </a>
      and included an address book, calendar, appointment scheduler, calculator, world time clock and notepad, utilizing its touch screen display.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The term "smart phone" appeared in print as early as 1995, describing AT&amp;T's PhoneWriter Communicator.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACM_Interactions_article_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ACM_Interactions_article-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (September 2016)">
          non-primary source needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="PDAs">
       PDAs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: PDAs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">
       Personal digital assistant
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the mid-late 1990s, many mobile phone users carried a separate dedicated PDA device, running early versions of operating systems such as
      <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">
       Palm OS
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_OS" title="BlackBerry OS">
       BlackBerry OS
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">
       Windows CE
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">
       Pocket PC
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phonescoop-smartphone_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-smartphone-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      These operating systems would later evolve into
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">
       mobile operating systems
      </a>
      . In March 1996,
      <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">
       Hewlett-Packard
      </a>
      released the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OmniGo_700LX" title="OmniGo 700LX">
       OmniGo 700LX
      </a>
      , a modified
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/200LX" title="200LX">
       200LX
      </a>
      PDA that supported a Nokia 2110-compatible phone with
      <a href="/wiki/Read-only_memory" title="Read-only memory">
       ROM
      </a>
      -based software to support it. It had a 640x200 resolution CGA compatible 4-shade gray-scale LCD screen and could be used to place and receive calls, and to create and receive text messages, emails and faxes. It was also 100% DOS 5.0 compatible, allowing it to run thousands of existing software titles, including early versions of Windows.
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 1996,
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
       Nokia
      </a>
      released the
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia_9000_Communicator" title="Nokia 9000 Communicator">
       Nokia 9000 Communicator
      </a>
      , a digital cellular phone based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia_2110" title="Nokia 2110">
       Nokia 2110
      </a>
      with an integrated
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">
       PDA
      </a>
      based on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GEOS_V3.0" title="GEOS V3.0">
       GEOS V3.0
      </a>
      operating system from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geoworks" title="Geoworks">
       Geoworks
      </a>
      . The two components were attached by a hinge in what became known as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clamshell_design" title="Clamshell design">
       clamshell design
      </a>
      , with the display above and a physical
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/QWERTY_keyboard" title="QWERTY keyboard">
       QWERTY keyboard
      </a>
      below. The PDA provided e-mail; calendar, address book, calculator and notebook applications; text-based Web browsing; and could send and receive faxes. When closed, the device could be used as a digital cellular phone. In June 1999
      <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">
       Qualcomm
      </a>
      released the "pdQ Smartphone", a
      <a href="/wiki/Code_division_multiple_access" title="Code division multiple access">
       CDMA
      </a>
      digital
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_Communications_Service" title="Personal Communications Service">
       PCS
      </a>
      Smartphone with an integrated Palm PDA and Internet connectivity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Subsequent landmark devices included:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_R380" title="Ericsson R380">
        Ericsson R380
       </a>
       (2000) by
       <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_Mobile_Communications" title="Ericsson Mobile Communications">
        Ericsson Mobile Communications
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first device marketed as a "smartphone",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it combined the functions of a mobile phone and PDA, and supported limited Web browsing with a
       <a href="/wiki/Resistive_touchscreen" title="Resistive touchscreen">
        resistive touchscreen
       </a>
       utilizing a
       <a href="/wiki/Stylus_(computing)" title="Stylus (computing)">
        stylus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kyocera_6035" title="Kyocera 6035">
        Kyocera 6035
       </a>
       (early 2001) introduced by
       <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc." title="Palm, Inc.">
        Palm, Inc.
       </a>
       Combining a PDA with a mobile phone, it operated on the
       <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">
        Verizon
       </a>
       network, and supported limited Web browsing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Handspring_(company)" title="Handspring (company)">
        Handspring
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Treo_180" title="Treo 180">
        Treo 180
       </a>
       (2002), the first smartphone to combine the
       <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">
        Palm OS
       </a>
       and a GSM phone with telephony, SMS messaging and Internet access fully integrated into the OS.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Smartphones before present-day Android-, iOS- and BlackBerry-based phones typically used the
      <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">
       Symbian
      </a>
      operating system. Originally developed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psion_(computers)" title="Psion (computers)">
       Psion
      </a>
      , it was the world's most widely used smartphone operating system until the last quarter of 2010.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_adoption">
       Mass adoption
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mass adoption">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1999, the Japanese firm
      <a href="/wiki/NTT_DoCoMo" title="NTT DoCoMo">
       NTT DoCoMo
      </a>
      released the first smartphones to achieve mass adoption within a country. These phones ran on
      <a href="/wiki/I-mode" title="I-mode">
       i-mode
      </a>
      , which provided data transmission speeds up to 9.6 kbit/s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Unlike future generations of wireless services, NTT DoCoMo's i-mode used
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CHTML" title="CHTML">
       cHTML
      </a>
      , a language which restricted some aspects of traditional
      <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">
       HTML
      </a>
      in favor of increasing data speed for the devices. Limited functionality, small screens and limited bandwidth allowed for phones to use the slower data speeds available.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The rise of i-mode helped NTT DoCoMo accumulate an estimated 40 million subscribers by the end of 2001. It was also ranked first in market capitalization in Japan and second globally. This power would wane in the face of the rise of 3G and new phones with advanced wireless network capabilities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Outside Japan smartphones were still rare until the introduction of the
      <a href="/wiki/Danger_Hiptop" title="Danger Hiptop">
       Danger Hiptop
      </a>
      in 2002, which saw moderate success in the US as the
      <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">
       T-Mobile
      </a>
      Sidekick. Later, in the mid-2000s, devices based on Microsoft's
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">
       Windows Mobile
      </a>
      started to gain popularity among business users in the U.S. The
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">
       BlackBerry
      </a>
      later gained mass adoption in the U.S., and American users popularized the term "CrackBerry" in 2006 due to its addictive nature.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The company first released its GSM BlackBerry 6210, BlackBerry 6220, and BlackBerry 6230 devices in 2003.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_systems">
       Operating systems
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Operating systems">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Symbian was the most popular smartphone OS in Europe during the middle to late 2000s. Initially, Nokia's Symbian devices were focused on business, similar to Windows Mobile and BlackBerry devices at the time. From 2006 onwards, Nokia started producing entertainment-focused smartphones, popularized by the
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Nseries" title="Nokia Nseries">
       Nseries
      </a>
      . In Asia, with the exception of Japan, the trend was similar to that of Europe.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      In 2003,
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">
       Motorola
      </a>
      launched the first smartphone to use
      <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">
       Linux
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola_A760" title="Motorola A760">
       A760
      </a>
      handset.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While the initial release was limited to a single high-end handset only available in the Asia-Pacific region, the maker's intention was to eventually use Linux on most of its handsets, including the lower-end models. Further models to use Linux such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Ming" title="Motorola Ming">
       Motorola Ming
      </a>
      A1200i in 2005 and several successors to the Ming line would be unveiled through 2010. In late 2009, Motorola released the
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Cliq" title="Motorola Cliq">
       Motorola Cliq
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      the first of Motorola's smartphones to run the Linux-based Android operating system.
     </p>
     <p>
      In early 2007,
      <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">
       Apple Inc.
      </a>
      introduced the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPhone_(original)" title="IPhone (original)">
       iPhone
      </a>
      , one of the first smartphones to use a
      <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">
       multi-touch
      </a>
      interface. The iPhone was notable for its use of a large touchscreen for direct finger input as its main means of interaction, instead of a stylus, keyboard, or keypad typical for smartphones at the time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iPhone-is-not_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-iPhone-is-not-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In October 2008, the first phone to use
      <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
       Android
      </a>
      called the
      <a href="/wiki/HTC_Dream" title="HTC Dream">
       HTC Dream
      </a>
      (also known as the T-Mobile G1) was released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_release_of_T-Mobile_G1_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UK_release_of_T-Mobile_G1-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T-Mobile_G1_Event_Round-up_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-T-Mobile_G1_Event_Round-up-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Android is an
      <a href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">
       open-source
      </a>
      platform founded by
      <a href="/wiki/Andy_Rubin" title="Andy Rubin">
       Andy Rubin
      </a>
      and now owned by
      <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
       Google
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-open-alliance_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-open-alliance-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-android-atlas_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-android-atlas-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although Android's adoption was relatively slow at first, it started to gain widespread popularity in 2010, and in early 2012 dominated the smartphone market share worldwide, which continues to this day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kantar_Worldpanel_Q3_2012_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kantar_Worldpanel_Q3_2012-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      These new platforms led to the decline of earlier ones.
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
       Microsoft
      </a>
      , for instance, started a new OS from scratch, called
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">
       Windows Phone
      </a>
      . Nokia abandoned Symbian and partnered with Microsoft to use Windows Phone on its smartphones. Windows Phone then became the third-most-popular OS. Palm's
      <a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">
       webOS
      </a>
      was bought by Hewlett-Packard and later sold to
      <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">
       LG Electronics
      </a>
      for use on LG
      <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">
       smart TVs
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Limited" title="BlackBerry Limited">
       BlackBerry Limited
      </a>
      , formerly known as Research In Motion, also made a new platform based on
      <a href="/wiki/QNX" title="QNX">
       QNX
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_10" title="BlackBerry 10">
       BlackBerry 10
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capacitive_touchscreen" title="Capacitive touchscreen">
       capacitive touchscreen
      </a>
      also changed smartphone
      <a href="/wiki/Form_factor_(mobile_phones)" title="Form factor (mobile phones)">
       form factors
      </a>
      . Before 2007, it was common for devices to have a physical numeric keypad or physical
      <a href="/wiki/QWERTY" title="QWERTY">
       QWERTY
      </a>
      keyboard in either a candybar or sliding form factor. However, by 2010, there were no top-selling smartphones with physical keypads.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2010s_technological_developments">
       2010s technological developments
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010s technological developments">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 2013, the
      <a href="/wiki/Fairphone" title="Fairphone">
       Fairphone
      </a>
      company launched its first "socially ethical" smartphone at the
      <a href="/wiki/London_Design_Festival" title="London Design Festival">
       London Design Festival
      </a>
      to address concerns regarding the sourcing of materials in the manufacturing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fair_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fair-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In late 2013, QSAlpha commenced production of a smartphone designed entirely around security, encryption and identity protection.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In December 2013, the world's first curved
      <a href="/wiki/OLED" title="OLED">
       OLED
      </a>
      technology smartphones were introduced to the retail market with the sale of the
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Round" title="Samsung Galaxy Round">
       Samsung Galaxy Round
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/LG_G_Flex" title="LG G Flex">
       LG G Flex
      </a>
      models.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Samsung phones with more bends and folds in the screens were expected in 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013, water and dustproofing have made their way into mainstream high end smartphones including
      <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z" title="Sony Xperia Z">
       Sony Xperia Z
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z3" title="Sony Xperia Z3">
       Sony Xperia Z3
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S5" title="Samsung Galaxy S5">
       Samsung Galaxy S5
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Previously, this feature was confined to special ruggedized phones designed for outdoor use.
     </p>
     <p>
      In early 2014, smartphones were beginning to use
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quad_HD" title="Quad HD">
       Quad HD
      </a>
      (2K) 2560x1440 on 5.5" screens with up to 534
      <a href="/wiki/Pixel_density" title="Pixel density">
       PPI
      </a>
      on devices such as the
      <a href="/wiki/LG_G3" title="LG G3">
       LG G3
      </a>
      which is a significant improvement over Apple's
      <a href="/wiki/Retina_Display" title="Retina Display">
       Retina Display
      </a>
      . Quad HD is used in advanced televisions and computer monitors, but with 110 ppi or less on such larger displays.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, Wi-Fi networks were used a lot for smartphones. As Wi-Fi became more prevalent and easier to connect to, it was predicted that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wi-Fi_phone" title="Wi-Fi phone">
       Wi-Fi phone
      </a>
      services will start to take off.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, LG introduced
      <a href="/wiki/Laser" title="Laser">
       lasers
      </a>
      on the LG G3 to help camera focus.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, some smartphones had such good digital cameras that they could be categorized as high-end
      <a href="/wiki/Point-and-shoot_camera" title="Point-and-shoot camera">
       point-and-shoot cameras
      </a>
      with large sensors up to 1" with 20
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megapixel" title="Megapixel">
       megapixels
      </a>
      and 4K video. Some can store their pictures in proprietary
      <a href="/wiki/Raw_image_format" title="Raw image format">
       raw image format
      </a>
      , but the Android (operating system) 5.0 Lollipop serves open source RAW images.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 2015, smartphones were increasingly integrated with everyday uses. For instance, credit cards,
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_payment" title="Mobile payment">
       mobile payments
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_banking" title="Mobile banking">
       mobile banking
      </a>
      were integrated into smartphone applications and Software as a Service (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SaaS" title="SaaS">
       SaaS
      </a>
      ) platforms.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, recent technological innovations are causing the role of traditional keys to be fused into the smartphones, because a smartphone can act as a digital key and access badge for its users.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In October 2015, Microsoft announced Windows Continuum, a feature that allows users to connect their devices to an external monitor via Microsoft Continuum Display Dock.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-windows.microsoft.com_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-windows.microsoft.com-50">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
      HP adds a layer to the Continuum with their HP Workplace which enables user to run a Win32 app by a virtualized server.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first
      <a href="/wiki/Modular_smartphone" title="Modular smartphone">
       modular smartphone
      </a>
      available to the public was the
      <a href="/wiki/Fairphone_2" title="Fairphone 2">
       Fairphone 2
      </a>
      , which was released in December 2015. Unlike most smartphones, users can remove and replace parts on this phone.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_possible_developments">
       Future possible developments
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Future possible developments">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Rollable_display" title="Rollable display">
       Foldable
      </a>
      OLED smartphones have been anticipated for years but have failed to materialize because of the relatively high failure rate when producing these screens.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      As well, creating a battery that can be folded is another hurdle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_operating_systems">
       Mobile operating systems
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mobile operating systems">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">
       Mobile operating system
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Android">
       Android
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Android">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
       Android (operating system)
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1080" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/220px-Android_6.0-en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/330px-Android_6.0-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/440px-Android_6.0-en.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Android is the top-selling smartphone OS in 2016.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gartner1_53-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gartner1-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IDCQ3_54-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-IDCQ3-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
      </b>
      is a mobile operating system developed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Inc." title="Google Inc.">
       Google Inc.
      </a>
      , and backed by an industry consortium known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Open_Handset_Alliance" title="Open Handset Alliance">
       Open Handset Alliance
      </a>
      . It is an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source_software" title="Open source software">
       open source
      </a>
      platform with optional
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
       proprietary
      </a>
      components, including a suite of flagship software for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_services" title="Google services">
       Google services
      </a>
      , and the application and content storefront
      <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">
       Google Play
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-irongrip_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ars-irongrip-55">
        [55]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Android was officially introduced via the release of its inaugural device, the
      <a href="/wiki/HTC_Dream" title="HTC Dream">
       HTC Dream
      </a>
      (T-Mobile G1) on 20 October 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet-tmobileretailer_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnet-tmobileretailer-56">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As an open source product, Android has also been the subject of third-party development. Development groups have used the Android source code to develop and distribute their own modified versions of the operating system, such as
      <a href="/wiki/CyanogenMod" title="CyanogenMod">
       CyanogenMod
      </a>
      , to add features to the OS and provide newer versions of Android to devices that no longer receive official updates from their vendor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianfrag_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-guardianfrag-57">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-c_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-c-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Software_fork" title="Software fork">
       Forked
      </a>
      versions of Android have also been adopted by other vendors, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">
       Amazon.com
      </a>
      , who used its "
      <a href="/wiki/Fire_OS" title="Fire OS">
       Fire OS
      </a>
      " on a range of
      <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">
       tablets
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Fire_Phone" title="Fire Phone">
       Fire Phone
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-fireosphone_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ars-fireosphone-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As it is a non-proprietary platform that has shipped on devices covering a wide range of market segments, Android has seen significant adoption.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gartner_Research" title="Gartner Research">
       Gartner Research
      </a>
      estimated that 325 million Android smartphones were sold during the fourth quarter of 2015, leading all other platforms.
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">
       Samsung Electronics
      </a>
      , who produces Android devices, was also the top smartphone vendor across all platforms in the same period of time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcw-androidshare_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcw-androidshare-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="iOS">
       iOS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: iOS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
       iOS
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IOS_10_Homescreen_iPhone_7.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="270" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/IOS_10_Homescreen_iPhone_7.png/220px-IOS_10_Homescreen_iPhone_7.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/57/IOS_10_Homescreen_iPhone_7.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IOS_10_Homescreen_iPhone_7.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Screenshot of IOS
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
        iOS
       </a>
      </b>
      (formerly
      <b>
       iPhone OS
      </b>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
       proprietary
      </a>
      mobile operating system developed by
      <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">
       Apple Inc.
      </a>
      primarily for its
      <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">
       iPhone
      </a>
      product line. The
      <a href="/wiki/IPhone_(1st_generation)" title="IPhone (1st generation)">
       iPhone
      </a>
      was first unveiled in January 2007. The device introduced numerous design concepts that have been adopted by modern smartphone platforms, such as the use of
      <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">
       multi-touch
      </a>
      gestures for navigation, eschewing physical controls such as physical keyboards in favor of those rendered by the operating system itself on its touchscreen (including the keyboard), and the use of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skeumorphism" title="Skeumorphism">
       skeumorphism
      </a>
      making features and controls within the user interface resemble real-world objects and concepts in order to improve their usability.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlantic-startover_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-atlantic-startover-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2008, Apple introduced the
      <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">
       App Store
      </a>
      , a centralized storefront for purchasing new software for iPhone devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj-breaking_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wsj-breaking-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet-iphonemetworld_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnet-iphonemetworld-66">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
      iOS can also integrate with Apple's desktop music program
      <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">
       iTunes
      </a>
      to sync media to a personal computer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The dependency on a PC was removed with the introduction of
      <a href="/wiki/ICloud" title="ICloud">
       iCloud
      </a>
      on later versions of iOS, which provides synchronization of user data via internet servers between multiple devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCWorld-icloud_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PCWorld-icloud-69">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The iPhone line's early dominance was credited with reshaping the smartphone industry, and helping make Apple one of the world's most valuable publicly traded companies by 2011. However, the iPhone and iOS have generally been in second place in worldwide market share.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcw-androidshare_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcw-androidshare-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales16_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales16-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Windows_Phone">
       Windows Phone
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Windows Phone">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">
       Windows Phone
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Windows_10_Mobile_homescreen.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="300" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/Windows_10_Mobile_homescreen.png/220px-Windows_10_Mobile_homescreen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/74/Windows_10_Mobile_homescreen.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Windows_10_Mobile_homescreen.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Smartphone OS by Microsoft.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       Windows Phone
      </b>
      is a series of
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
       proprietary
      </a>
      smartphone operating systems developed by
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
       Microsoft
      </a>
      . Its original release,
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_7" title="Windows Phone 7">
       Windows Phone 7
      </a>
      , was a revamped version of the previous,
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">
       Windows CE
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">
       Windows Mobile
      </a>
      platform; however, it was incompatible with the legacy platform.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eWeek_Explains_72-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-eWeek_Explains-72">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Windows Phone's user interface was designed to contrast with its competitors, utilizing a design language codenamed "
      <a href="/wiki/Metro_(design_language)" title="Metro (design language)">
       Metro
      </a>
      " which de-emphasized
      <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">
       iconography
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skeuomorphism" title="Skeuomorphism">
       skeuomorphism
      </a>
      in favor of flat, text-based designs. The platform also featured concepts such as "live tiles" on its home screen that can display dynamic content, and "Hubs"which aggregate content from various sources and services (such as a user's local contacts, in combination with connected
      <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">
       social networking services
      </a>
      ) into unified displays. Windows Phone also integrated with other Microsoft brands and platforms, including
      <a href="/wiki/Bing" title="Bing">
       Bing
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/OneDrive" title="OneDrive">
       SkyDrive
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">
       Xbox
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_Mobile" title="Microsoft Office Mobile">
       Microsoft Office Mobile
      </a>
      apps were also bundled with the operating system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_8" title="Windows Phone 8">
       Windows Phone 8
      </a>
      was released in 2012; it was incompatible with existing devices, but switched to a core system based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">
       Windows NT
      </a>
      platform, expanded the platform's hardware support and functionality, and added expanded enterprise-oriented functionality such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drive_encryption" title="Drive encryption">
       storage encryption
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp8-theverge_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wp8-theverge-76">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_10_Mobile" title="Windows 10 Mobile">
       Windows 10 Mobile
      </a>
      was released in late-2015; it is no longer promoted under the Windows Phone brand, as it is intended to provide greater consistency and integration with
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">
       Windows 10
      </a>
      for PC, including cross-platform applications via
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Windows_Platform" title="Universal Windows Platform">
       Universal Windows Platform
      </a>
      , and the ability to
      <a href="/wiki/Docking_station" title="Docking station">
       dock
      </a>
      supported devices to use a
      <a href="/wiki/Desktop_metaphor" title="Desktop metaphor">
       desktop
      </a>
      interface with keyboard and mouse support.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-displaydock_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-displaydock-79">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-universalpreview_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-universalpreview-80">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-almostevery_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ars-almostevery-81">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Windows Phone series has had poor adoption in comparison to its competitors. Lack of interest in the platform also led to a decrease in third-party applications, and some vendors ended their support for Windows Phone altogether.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcw-androidshare_62-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcw-androidshare-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-wpisdead_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-wpisdead-82">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-evaporatingwp_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-evaporatingwp-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The most prominent Windows Phone vendor was
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
       Nokia
      </a>
      , who exclusively adopted Windows Phone as its smartphone platform in 2011 as part of a wider partnership with Microsoft.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstechnica-ms_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-arstechnica-ms-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nokia's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lumia_series" title="Lumia series">
       Lumia series
      </a>
      was the most popular line of Windows Phone devices, representing 83.3% of all Windows Phones sold in June 2013,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetaNewsNokiaMarketshare_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BetaNewsNokiaMarketshare-85">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Microsoft acquired Nokia's mobile business for just over 5.44 billion in April 2014, forming the subsidiary
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Mobile" title="Microsoft Mobile">
       Microsoft Mobile
      </a>
      under former Nokia CEO
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Elop" title="Stephen Elop">
       Stephen Elop
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet_phone_div_sold_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnet_phone_div_sold-86">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph-msmobile_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph-msmobile-87">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-closedate_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-verge-closedate-88">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="BlackBerry">
       BlackBerry
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: BlackBerry">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">
       BlackBerry
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackBerry_Classic.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1913" data-file-width="1255" height="335" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/BlackBerry_Classic.png/220px-BlackBerry_Classic.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/BlackBerry_Classic.png/330px-BlackBerry_Classic.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/BlackBerry_Classic.png/440px-BlackBerry_Classic.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlackBerry_Classic.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A Blackberry Classic smartphone with an integrated keyboard
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1999,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_In_Motion" title="Research In Motion">
       RIM
      </a>
      released its first BlackBerry devices, providing secure real-time push-email communications on wireless devices. Services such as BlackBerry Messenger provide the integration of all communications into a single inbox. In September 2012, RIM announced that the 200 millionth BlackBerry smartphone was shipped. As of September 2014, there were around 46 million active BlackBerry service subscribers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most recently, RIM has undergone a platform transition, changing its name to BlackBerry and making new devices on a new platform named "BlackBerry 10"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in November 2015 released an Android smartphone, the
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Priv" title="BlackBerry Priv">
       BlackBerry Priv
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sailfish_OS">
       Sailfish OS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sailfish OS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Sailfish_OS" title="Sailfish OS">
       Sailfish OS
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Sailfish OS is based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">
       Linux kernel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mer_(software_distribution)" title="Mer (software distribution)">
       Mer
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally Sailfish OS includes a partially or completely
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
       proprietary
      </a>
      multi-tasking
      <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">
       user interface
      </a>
      programmed by
      <a href="/wiki/Jolla" title="Jolla">
       Jolla
      </a>
      . This user interface differentiate Jolla smartphones from others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sailfish OS is intended to be a system made by many of the MeeGo team, which left Nokia to form Jolla, utilizing funding from Nokia's "Bridge" program which helps establish and support start-up companies formed by ex-Nokia employees.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tizen">
       Tizen
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tizen">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Tizen" title="Tizen">
       Tizen
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Tizen is a Linux-based
      <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">
       operating system
      </a>
      for devices, including smartphones,
      <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">
       tablets
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_car_entertainment" title="In car entertainment">
       in-vehicle infotainment
      </a>
      (IVI) devices, smart TVs,
      <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">
       laptops
      </a>
      and smart cameras. Tizen is a project within the
      <a href="/wiki/Linux_Foundation" title="Linux Foundation">
       Linux Foundation
      </a>
      and is governed by a Technical Steering Group (TSG) composed of Samsung and Intel among others. In April 2014, Samsung released the Samsung Gear 2 and the Gear 2 Neo, running Tizen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Z1" title="Samsung Z1">
       Samsung Z1
      </a>
      is the first smartphone produced by Samsung that runs Tizen; it was released in the
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       Indian
      </a>
      market on January 14, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ubuntu_Touch">
       Ubuntu Touch
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ubuntu Touch">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Touch" title="Ubuntu Touch">
       Ubuntu Touch
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       Ubuntu Touch
      </b>
      (also known as
      <b>
       Ubuntu Phone
      </b>
      ) is a mobile version of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ubuntu_operating_system" title="Ubuntu operating system">
       Ubuntu operating system
      </a>
      developed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_Ltd" title="Canonical Ltd">
       Canonical UK Ltd
      </a>
      and Ubuntu Community.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-backed_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-backed-99">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is designed primarily for touchscreen mobile devices such as smartphones and tablet computers.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinued_operating_systems">
       Discontinued operating systems
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Discontinued operating systems">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Symbian">
       Symbian
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Symbian">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">
       Symbian
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Symbian was originally developed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psion_(computers)" title="Psion (computers)">
       Psion
      </a>
      as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EPOC32" title="EPOC32">
       EPOC32
      </a>
      . It was the world's most widely used smartphone operating system until Q4 2010, though the platform never gained popularity in the U.S., as it did in Europe and Asia. The first Symbian phone, the touchscreen Ericsson R380 Smartphone, was released in 2000,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was the first device marketed as a "smartphone".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It combined a PDA with a mobile phone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Variants of Symbian OS began to emerge, most notably Symbian UIQ, MOAP and S60, each supported by different manufacturers. With the creation of Symbian Foundation in 2008, Symbian OS was unified under one variant under the stewardship of Nokia. In February 2011, Nokia announced that it would replace Symbian with Windows Phone as the operating system on all of its future smartphones, with the platform being abandoned over the following few years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NokiaWinPho7_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NokiaWinPho7-104">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Windows_Mobile">
       Windows Mobile
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Windows Mobile">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">
       Windows Mobile
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Windows Mobile was based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">
       Windows CE
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Kernel_(operating_system)" title="Kernel (operating system)">
       kernel
      </a>
      and first appeared as the
      <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">
       Pocket PC
      </a>
      2000 operating system. Throughout its lifespan, the operating system was available in both touchscreen and non-touchscreen formats. It was supplied with a suite of applications developed with the Microsoft Windows API and was designed to have features and appearance somewhat similar to desktop versions of Windows. Third parties could develop software for Windows Mobile with no restrictions imposed by Microsoft. Software applications were eventually purchasable from Windows Marketplace for Mobile during the service's brief lifespan. Windows Mobile was eventually phased out in favor of
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">
       Windows Phone
      </a>
      OS.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bada">
       Bada
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bada">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Bada" title="Bada">
       Bada
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Bada operating system for smartphones was announced by Samsung in November 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first Bada-based phone was the
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Wave_S8500" title="Samsung Wave S8500">
       Samsung Wave S8500
      </a>
      , released in June 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Samsung shipped 4.5 million phones running Bada in Q2 of 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013, Bada merged with a similar platform called Tizen.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_OS">
       Firefox OS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Firefox OS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">
       Firefox OS
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">
       Firefox OS
      </a>
      was demonstrated by
      <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">
       Mozilla
      </a>
      in February 2012. It was designed to have a complete community-based alternative system for mobile devices, using open standards and
      <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">
       HTML5
      </a>
      applications. The first commercially available Firefox OS phones were ZTE Open and Alcatel
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=One_Touch_Fire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="One Touch Fire (page does not exist)">
       One Touch Fire
      </a>
      . As of 2014, more companies have partnered with Mozilla including
      <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">
       Panasonic
      </a>
      (which is making a
      <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">
       smart TV
      </a>
      with Firefox OS) and Sony.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In December 2015, Mozilla announced that it would phase out development of Firefox OS for smartphones, and would reposition the project to focus on other forms of Internet-connected devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ndtv-killedfxos_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ndtv-killedfxos-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Palm_OS">
       Palm OS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Palm OS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">
       Palm OS
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In late 2001,
      <a href="/wiki/Handspring_(company)" title="Handspring (company)">
       Handspring
      </a>
      launched the
      <a href="/wiki/Springboard_Expansion_Slot" title="Springboard Expansion Slot">
       Springboard
      </a>
      GSM phone module with limited success. In May 2002, Handspring released the Palm OS
      <a href="/wiki/Treo_270" title="Treo 270">
       Treo 270
      </a>
      smartphone, that did not support Springboard, with both a touchscreen and a full keyboard. The Treo had wireless web browsing, email, calendar, a contact organizer and mobile third-party applications that could be downloaded or synced with a computer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Handspring was purchased by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc" title="Palm, Inc">
       Palm, Inc
      </a>
      which released the
      <a href="/wiki/Treo_600" title="Treo 600">
       Treo 600
      </a>
      and continued releasing Treo devices with a few Treo devices using Windows Mobile. After buying Palm in 2011, Hewlett-Packard (HP) discontinued its webOS smartphone and tablet production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="webOS">
       webOS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: webOS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">
       webOS
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      webOS is a proprietary mobile operating system running on the Linux kernel, initially developed by Palm, which launched with the
      <a href="/wiki/Palm_Pre" title="Palm Pre">
       Palm Pre
      </a>
      . After being acquired by HP, two phones (the
      <a href="/wiki/HP_Veer" title="HP Veer">
       Veer
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/HP_Pre_3" title="HP Pre 3">
       Pre 3
      </a>
      ) and a tablet (the
