      <a href="/wiki/HP_TouchPad" title="HP TouchPad">
       TouchPad
      </a>
      ) running webOS were introduced in 2011. On August 18, 2011, HP announced that webOS hardware was to be discontinued
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      but would continue to support and update webOS software and develop the webOS ecosystem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      HP released webOS as open source under the name Open webOS, and plans to update it with additional features.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 25, 2013 HP announced the sale of WebOS to LG Electronics, who used the operating system for its current "smart" or Internet-connected TVs, but not smartphones. In January 2014,
      <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">
       Qualcomm
      </a>
      has announced that it has acquired technology patents from HP, which includes all the WebOS patents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Maemo_.2F_MeeGo">
       Maemo / MeeGo
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Maemo / MeeGo">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/MeeGo" title="MeeGo">
       MeeGo
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      MeeGo is an operating system created from the source code of
      <a href="/wiki/Moblin" title="Moblin">
       Moblin
      </a>
      (produced by Intel) and
      <a href="/wiki/Maemo" title="Maemo">
       Maemo
      </a>
      (produced by Nokia). Before that, Nokia used Maemo on some of its smartphones and internet tablets (such as Nokia N810 and N900). MeeGo was originally envisioned to power a variety of devices from netbooks, tablets to smartphones and smart TVs. However, the only smartphones which used MeeGo was the
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia_N9" title="Nokia N9">
       Nokia N9
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia_N950" title="Nokia N950">
       Nokia N950
      </a>
      (MeeGo v1.2 Harmattan). Following Nokia's decision to move to Windows Phone OS in 2011 and to cease MeeGo development, the Linux Foundation canceled MeeGo in September 2011 in favor of the development of Tizen.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Application_stores">
       Application stores
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Application stores">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices">
       List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The introduction of Apple's App Store for the iPhone and iPod Touch in July 2008 popularized manufacturer-hosted
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices">
       online distribution
      </a>
      for third-party applications (
      <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">
       software
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_programs" title="Computer programs">
       computer programs
      </a>
      ) focused on a single platform. There are a huge variety of apps, including
      <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">
       video games
      </a>
      , music products and business tools. Up until that point, smartphone application distribution depended on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices#Third-party_platforms" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices">
       third-party sources
      </a>
      providing applications for multiple platforms, such as
      <a href="/wiki/GetJar" title="GetJar">
       GetJar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Handango" title="Handango">
       Handango
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Handmark" title="Handmark">
       Handmark
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PocketGear" title="PocketGear">
       PocketGear
      </a>
      . Following the success of the App Store, other smartphone manufacturers launched application stores, such as Google's Android Market (now
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Play_Store" title="Google Play Store">
       Google Play Store
      </a>
      ) and RIM's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BlackBerry_App_World" title="BlackBerry App World">
       BlackBerry App World
      </a>
      in April 2009. In February 2014, 93% of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_developers" title="Mobile developers">
       mobile developers
      </a>
      were targeting smartphones first for mobile app development.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Display">
       Display
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Display">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Display_device" title="Display device">
       Display device
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="834" data-file-width="1178" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png/220px-Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png/330px-Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png/440px-Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Galaxy_S6_S6_Edge_and_S6_Edge_Plus.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S6" title="Samsung Galaxy S6">
         Samsung Galaxy S6
        </a>
        (5.1 inches), S6 Edge(5.1 inches), S6 Edge+(5.7 inches)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      One of the main characteristics of smartphones is their
      <a href="/wiki/Display_device" title="Display device">
       screen
      </a>
      . It usually fills most of the phone's front surface (about 70%); screen size usually defines the size of a smartphone. Many have an
      <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio" title="Aspect ratio">
       aspect ratio
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">
       16:9
      </a>
      ; some are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4:3" title="4:3">
       4:3
      </a>
      or other ratios. They are measured in diagonal
      <a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">
       inches
      </a>
      , starting from 2.45 inches.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Phones with screens larger than 5.2 inches are often called "
      <a href="/wiki/Phablet" title="Phablet">
       phablets
      </a>
      ". Smartphones with screens over 4.5 inches commonly are shifted while using a single hand, since most thumbs cannot reach the entire screen surface, or used in place with both hands.
      <a href="/wiki/Liquid-crystal_display" title="Liquid-crystal display">
       Liquid-crystal displays
      </a>
      are the most common; others are
      <a href="/wiki/IPS_panel" title="IPS panel">
       IPS
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LED" title="LED">
       LED
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/OLED" title="OLED">
       OLED
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/AMOLED" title="AMOLED">
       AMOLED
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/E_Ink" title="E Ink">
       E Ink
      </a>
      displays. In the 2010s,
      <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">
       Braille
      </a>
      screens, which can be used by visually impaired people are being developed. It is expected that Braille screens will use some type of
      <a href="/wiki/Microfluidics" title="Microfluidics">
       microfluidics
      </a>
      technology.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Accessories">
       Accessories
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Accessories">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eagletechz_case.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="729" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Eagletechz_case.jpg/200px-Eagletechz_case.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Eagletechz_case.jpg/300px-Eagletechz_case.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Eagletechz_case.jpg/400px-Eagletechz_case.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eagletechz_case.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A selection of protective cases. The small cut-out in the left-hand corner is to enable the person to use the
        <a href="/wiki/Digital_camera" title="Digital camera">
         digital camera
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellphone" title="Cellphone">
       cellphones
      </a>
      , a range of accessories are sold for smartphones, including cases, screen protectors, power charging cables, add-on batteries, headphones, combined headphone-microphones which allow a person to use the phone without holding it to the ear, and
      <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">
       Bluetooth
      </a>
      -enabled
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powered_speaker" title="Powered speaker">
       powered speakers
      </a>
      that enable users to listen to music files stored on their smartphones. Cases range from relatively inexpensive rubber or soft plastic cases which provide moderate protection from bumps and good protection from scratches to more expensive, heavy-duty cases that combine a rubber padding with a hard outer shell. Some cases have a "book"-like form, with a cover that the user opens to use the device; when the cover is closed, it protects the screen. Some "book"-like cases have additional pockets for credit cards, thus enabling people to use them as
      <a href="/wiki/Wallet" title="Wallet">
       wallets
      </a>
      . Accessories include products sold by the manufacturer of the smartphone and compatible products made by other manufacturers.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Market_share">
       Market share
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Market share">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Usage">
       Usage
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Usage">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In the third quarter of 2012, one billion smartphones were in use worldwide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Don_Reisinger_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Don_Reisinger-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Global smartphone sales surpassed the sales figures for feature phones in early 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news1_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-news1-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2013, 65 percent of U.S. mobile consumers own smartphones.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jon_Fingas_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jon_Fingas-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The European mobile device market as of 2013 is 860 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In China, smartphones represented more than half of all handset shipments in the second quarter of 2012
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in 2014 there were 519.7 million smartphone users, with the number estimated to grow to 700 million by 2018.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of November 2011, 27% of all photographs were taken with camera-equipped smartphones.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A study conducted in September 2012 concluded that 4 out of 5 smartphone owners use the device to shop.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another study conducted in June 2013 concluded that 56% of American adults now owned a smartphone of some kind. Android and iPhone owners account for half of the cell phone user population. Higher income adults and those under age 35 lead the way when it comes to smartphone ownership.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Worldwide shipments of smartphones topped 1 billion units in 2013, up 38% from 2012's 725 million, while comprising a 55% share of the mobile phone market in 2013, up from 42% in 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since 1996, smartphone shipments have had positive growth, but in Q1 2016 for the first time the shipments dropped by 3 percent
      <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/year-over-year" title="wikt:year-over-year">
       year on year
      </a>
      . The situation was caused by the maturing China market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="By_manufacturer">
       By manufacturer
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: By manufacturer">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:341px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smartphones_back.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/339px-Smartphones_back.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/509px-Smartphones_back.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/678px-Smartphones_back.jpg 2x" width="339"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smartphones_back.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/LG_G3" title="LG G3">
         LG G3
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/OnePlus_One" title="OnePlus One">
         OnePlus One
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_4" title="Samsung Galaxy Note 4">
         Samsung Galaxy Note 4
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPhone_6_Plus" title="IPhone 6 Plus">
         iPhone 6 Plus
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>

      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      In 2011, Samsung had the highest shipment
      <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">
       market share
      </a>
      worldwide, followed by Apple. In 2013, Samsung had 31.3% market share, a slight increase from 30.3% in 2012, while Apple was at 15.3%, a decrease from 18.7% in 2012. Huawei, LG and Lenovo were at about 5% each, significantly better than 2012 figures, while others had about 40%, the same as the previous years figure. Only Apple lost market share, although their shipment volume still increased by 12.9 percent; the rest had significant increases in shipment volumes of 36 to 92 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Q1 2014, Samsung had a 31% share and Apple had 16%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Q4 2014, Apple had a 20.4% share and Samsung had 19.9%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brett_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-brett-133">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In January 2015 in the US, Android market share was 53.2%, Apple's iOS had a 41.3% share and Samsung's Android smartphones had 29.3%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ComScore1_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ComScore1-134">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In January 2016, the US market share for Android smartphones was 52.8%, Apple had 43.6% share, Microsoft had 2.7% and BlackBerry had 0.8 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan2016_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jan2016-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">

       </td>
       <td>
        0.1%
       </td>
       <td>
        0.2%
       </td>
       <td>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gartner2_135-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gartner2-135">
          [135]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The market has been dominated by the Android operating system since 2010. Android's market share (measured by units shipment) rose from 33.2% in Q4 2011 to 78.1% of the market in Q4 2013. Apple's market share oscillated between 15% to 20.9% during the same period. BlackBerry's market share fell from 14.3% in Q4 2011 to 0.6% in Q4 2013. Windows Mobile market share rose from 1.5% to 3% during the same time frame.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_market_share_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-2014_market_share-136">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of the end of Q3 2014, Android was the most popular operating system, with a 84.4% market share, followed by iOS with 11.7%, Windows Phone with 2.9%, BlackBerry with 0.5% and all others with 0.6%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">
       Issues
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Issues">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Smartphones have presented issues similar to those affecting other
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_telephone" title="Mobile telephone">
       mobile telephones
      </a>
      . As well, there are some issues which are unique to smartphones.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_life">
       Battery life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Battery life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USB_battery_charger.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3096" data-file-width="4314" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/220px-USB_battery_charger.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/330px-USB_battery_charger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/440px-USB_battery_charger.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USB_battery_charger.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A high-capacity portable battery charger.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Compared to earlier non-smartphone mobile phones, smartphone battery life has generally been poor, due to the significant power requirements of their computer systems and color screens. Poor smartphone battery life has negatively affected customer satisfaction.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        [138]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        [139]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
      There is also a trend towards using batteries that the user cannot replace.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        [141]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smartphone users have addressed the challenge of limited battery life by purchasing additional chargers for use outside the home, at work, and in cars and by buying portable external "battery packs". External battery packs include generic models which are connected to the smartphone with a cable and custom-made models which "piggyback" onto a smartphone's case.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social">
       Social
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Social">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_overuse" title="Mobile phone overuse">
       Mobile phone overuse
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A 2012
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">
       University of Southern California
      </a>
      study found that
      <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">
       unprotected
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Adolescent_sexuality" title="Adolescent sexuality">
       adolescent sexual
      </a>
      activity was more common among owners of smartphones.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A study conducted by the
      <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">
       Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute
      </a>
      's (RPI) Lighting Research Center (LRC) concluded that smartphones, or any backlit devices, can seriously affect
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stages_of_sleep" title="Stages of sleep">
       sleep cycles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colaner_143-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Colaner-143">
        [143]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some persons might become psychologically attached to cellphones resulting in anxiety when separated from the devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        [144]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smombie" title="Smombie">
       smombie
      </a>
      " (a combination of "smartphone" and "
      <a href="/wiki/Zombie" title="Zombie">
       zombie
      </a>
      ") is a walking person using a smartphone and not paying attention as they walk, possibly risking an accident in the process, an increasing social phenomenon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sunday-times_145-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sunday-times-145">
        [145]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The issue of slow-moving smartphone users led to the temporary creation of a "mobile lane" for walking in
      <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">
       Chongqing
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_146-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbc-146">
        [146]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The issue of distracted smartphone users led the city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augsburg,_Germany" title="Augsburg, Germany">
       Augsburg, Germany
      </a>
      to embed pedestrian traffic lights in the pavement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        [147]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="While_driving">
       While driving
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: While driving">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phones_and_driving_safety" title="Mobile phones and driving safety">
       Mobile phones and driving safety
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Texting_while_driving" title="Texting while driving">
       Texting while driving
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/220px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/330px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/440px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
         New York City
        </a>
        driver using two handheld mobile phones at once.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Mobile phone use while driving, including talking on the phone, texting, or operating other phone features, is common but controversial. It is widely considered dangerous due to
      <a href="/wiki/Distracted_driving" title="Distracted driving">
       distracted driving
      </a>
      . Being distracted while operating a motor vehicle has been shown to increase the risk of accidents. In September 2010, the US
      <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">
       National Highway Traffic Safety Administration
      </a>
      (NHTSA) reported that 995 people were killed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restrictions_on_cell_phone_use_by_US_drivers" title="Restrictions on cell phone use by US drivers">
       drivers distracted by cell phones
      </a>
      . In March 2011 a US insurance company,
      <a href="/wiki/State_Farm_Insurance" title="State Farm Insurance">
       State Farm Insurance
      </a>
      , announced the results of a study which showed 19% of drivers surveyed accessed the Internet on a smartphone while driving.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-post-148">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many jurisdictions prohibit the use of mobile phones while driving. In Egypt, Israel, Japan, Portugal and Singapore, both handheld and hands-free use of a mobile phone (which uses a
      <a href="/wiki/Speakerphone" title="Speakerphone">
       speakerphone
      </a>
      ) is banned. In other countries including the UK and France and in many
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restrictions_on_cell_phone_use_by_US_drivers" title="Restrictions on cell phone use by US drivers">
       U.S. states
      </a>
      , only handheld phone use is banned, while hands-free use is permitted.
     </p>
     <p>
      A 2011 study reported that over 90% of college students surveyed text (initiate, reply or read) while driving.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        [149]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The scientific literature on the dangers of driving while sending a text message from a mobile phone, or
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Texting_while_driving" title="Texting while driving">
        texting while driving
       </a>
      </i>
      , is limited. A simulation study at the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah" title="University of Utah">
       University of Utah
      </a>
      found a sixfold increase in distraction-related accidents when texting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        [150]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to the increasing complexity of smartphones, this has introduced additional difficulties for law enforcement officials when attempting to distinguish one usage from another in drivers using their devices. This is more apparent in countries which ban both handheld and hands-free usage, rather than those which ban handheld use only, as officials cannot easily tell which function of the mobile phone is being used simply by looking at the driver. This can lead to drivers being stopped for using their device illegally for a phone call when, in fact, they were using the device legally, for example, when using the phone's incorporated controls for car stereo,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">
       GPS
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satnav" title="Satnav">
       satnav
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/220px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/330px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/440px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A sign along
        <a href="/wiki/Bellaire_Boulevard" title="Bellaire Boulevard">
         Bellaire Boulevard
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Southside_Place,_Texas" title="Southside Place, Texas">
         Southside Place, Texas
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">
         Greater Houston
        </a>
        ) states that using mobile phones while driving is prohibited from 7:30 am to 9:30 am and from 2:00 pm to 4:15 pm
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A 2010 study reviewed the incidence of mobile phone use while
      <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">
       cycling
      </a>
      and its effects on behaviour and safety.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        [151]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013 a national survey in the US reported the number of drivers who reported using their cellphones to access the Internet while driving had risen to nearly one of four.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A study conducted by the University of Illinois examined approaches for reducing inappropriate and problematic use of mobile phones, such as using mobile phones while driving.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        [153]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Accidents involving a driver being distracted by talking on a mobile phone have begun to be prosecuted as negligence similar to speeding. In the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      , from 27 February 2007, motorists who are caught using a hand-held mobile phone while driving will have three penalty points added to their license in addition to the fine of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C2%A3" title="">
       
      </a>
      60.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_154-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC-154">
        [154]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This increase was introduced to try to stem the increase in drivers ignoring the law.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2_155-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC2-155">
        [155]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
       Japan
      </a>
      prohibits all mobile phone use while driving, including use of hands-free devices. New Zealand has banned hand held cellphone use since 1 November 2009. Many states in the United States have banned texting on cell phones while driving. Illinois became the 17th American state to enforce this law.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_156-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-156">
        [156]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of July 2010, 30 states had banned texting while driving, with Kentucky becoming the most recent addition on July 15.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courier-Journal_157-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Courier-Journal-157">
        [157]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Public_Health_Law_Research&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Public Health Law Research (page does not exist)">
       Public Health Law Research
      </a>
      maintains a list of distracted driving laws in the United States. This database of laws provides a comprehensive view of the provisions of laws that restrict the use of mobile communication devices while driving for all 50 states and the District of Columbia between 1992, when first law was passed through December 1, 2010. The dataset contains information on 22 dichotomous, continuous or categorical variables including, for example, activities regulated (e.g., texting versus talking, hands-free versus handheld), targeted populations, and exemptions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        [158]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal">
       Legal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Legal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smartphone_wars" title="Smartphone wars">
       Smartphone wars
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A "patent war" between Samsung and Apple started when the latter claimed that the original
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S" title="Samsung Galaxy S">
       Galaxy S
      </a>
      Android phone copied the interfaceand possibly the hardwareof Apple's iOS for the
      <a href="/wiki/IPhone_3GS" title="IPhone 3GS">
       iPhone 3GS
      </a>
      . There was also smartphone patents licensing and litigation involving
      <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">
       Sony
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
       Google
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">
       Apple Inc.
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">
       Samsung
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
       Microsoft
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
       Nokia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">
       Motorola
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">
       Huawei
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/HTC" title="HTC">
       HTC
      </a>
      , among others. The conflict is part of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technology_patent_wars" title="Technology patent wars">
       wider "patent wars"
      </a>
      between multinational technology and software corporations. To secure and increase their
      <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">
       market share
      </a>
      , companies granted a
      <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">
       patent
      </a>
      can sue to prevent competitors from using the methods the patent covers. Since 2010 the number of lawsuits, counter-suits, and trade complaints based on patents and
      <a href="/wiki/Industrial_design_right" title="Industrial design right">
       designs
      </a>
      in the market for smartphones, and devices based on
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">
       smartphone OSes
      </a>
      such as
      <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
       Android
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
       iOS
      </a>
      , has increased significantly. Initial suits, countersuits, rulings, licence agreements, and other major events began in 2009 as the smartphone market grew more rapidly.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Medical">
       Medical
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Medical">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">
       Mobile app
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      With the rise in number of mobile medical apps in the market place, government regulatory agencies raised concerns on the safety of the use of such applications. These concerns were transformed into regulation initiatives worldwide with the aim of safeguarding users from untrusted medical advice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        [159]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Security">
       Security
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Security">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_security" title="Mobile security">
       Mobile security
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">
       Malware
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_virus" title="Mobile virus">
       Mobile virus
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Media_Transfer_Protocol" title="Media Transfer Protocol">
       Media Transfer Protocol
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Smartphone malware is easily distributed through an insecure
      <a href="/wiki/App_store" title="App store">
       app store
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juniper-malware_160-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Juniper-malware-160">
        [160]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trustbus11_161-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-trustbus11-161">
        [161]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Often malware is hidden in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement_of_software" title="Copyright infringement of software">
       pirated
      </a>
      versions of legitimate apps, which are then distributed through third-party app stores.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        [162]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        [163]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Malware risk also comes from what's known as an "update attack", where a legitimate application is later changed to include a malware component, which users then install when they are notified that the app has been updated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lookout-malware_164-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lookout-malware-164">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As well, one out of three robberies in 2012 in the United States involved the theft of a mobile phone. An online petition has urged smartphone makers to install
      <a href="/wiki/Kill_switch" title="Kill switch">
       kill switches
      </a>
      in their devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, Apple's "Find my iPhone" and Google's "Android Device Manager" can disable phones that have been lost/stolen. With BlackBerry Protect in OS version 10.3.2, devices can be rendered unrecoverable to even BlackBerry's own Operating System recovery tools if incorrectly authenticated or dissociated from their account.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        [166]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep">
       Sleep
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sleep">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electronic_media_and_sleep" title="Electronic media and sleep">
       Electronic media and sleep
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Using smartphones late at night can disturb sleep, due to the brightly lit screen affecting
      <a href="/wiki/Melatonin" title="Melatonin">
       melatonin
      </a>
      levels and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleep_cycles" title="Sleep cycles">
       sleep cycles
      </a>
      . In an effort to alleviate these issues, several apps that change the
      <a href="/wiki/Color_temperature" title="Color temperature">
       color temperature
      </a>
      of a screen to a warmer hue based on the time of day to reduce the amount of blue light generated have been developed for Android, while
      <a href="/wiki/IOS_9" title="IOS 9">
       iOS 9.3
      </a>
      integrated similar, system-level functionality known as "Night Shift". Amazon released a feature known as "blue shade" in their Fire OS "Bellini" 5.0 and later. It has also been theorized that for some users, addicted use of their phones, especially before they go to bed, can result in "
      <a href="/wiki/Ego_depletion" title="Ego depletion">
       ego depletion
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet-bluelight_167-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnet-bluelight-167">
        [167]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        [168]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        [169]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        [170]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_terms">
       Other terms
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Other terms">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Phablet" title="Phablet">
       Phablet
      </a>
      ", a
      <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">
       portmanteau
      </a>
      of the words
      <i>
       phone
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       tablet
      </i>
      , describes smartphones with larger screens.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes_172-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-forbes-172">
        [172]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcmag_173-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcmag-173">
        [173]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      "Superphone" is also used by some companies to market phones with unusually large screens and other expensive features.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        [174]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        [175]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
